## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and current concentration, which is the fundamental problem of chemical kinetics rate law determination. The dependence on both A and t suggests either a non-elementary rate law or time-dependent external forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics / saturation kinetics)
- Competitive inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combined first and second order)
- Time-dependent forcing with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (rate with time-dependent source)
- Oscillatory forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (periodic external influence)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction kinetics)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)
- Damped reaction with memory: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-modulated rate constant)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Simple integer power dependence on concentration (A, A^2, A^3) corresponds to molecularity of elementary reaction steps
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(K+A)) indicate enzyme-like saturation where a catalyst or surface site is limiting
- Negative constant terms added to concentration-dependent rates suggest equilibrium/reversible reactions with back-reaction contributions
- Product of A with (constant - A) terms indicates autocatalytic or logistic growth where both reactant and product participate
- Explicit time dependence in rate expressions (beyond through A) suggests external forcing, photolysis, or temperature ramping
- Square in the denominator (1+A)^2 suggests bimolecular surface adsorption or competitive dual-site mechanisms
- Sum of power-law terms (c0*A^n + c1*A^m) indicates parallel reaction pathways with different orders
- Exponential dependence on time multiplied by concentration suggests a time-varying rate constant (e.g., temperature ramp via Arrhenius)
